  - **HR AI** (#end_hr): Recruitment, onboarding.
  - **Customer Service AI** (#end_customer_service): Inquiry automation, support ticketing.
- **Standalone Products** (#end_standalone)
  - Each AI agent offered separately (e.g., Sales AI at $99/month).
  - Licensing for enterprises (e.g., Emaar, Hilton).
- **Global Reach** (#end_global)
  - 2,500 customers across Dubai, US, UK, Singapore, China, India.
  - Compliance: GDPR, CCPA, UAE laws.
- **Revenue**: $10M, 70–80% SaaS margins, 5–10x ROI for investors.

## Step-by-Step Figma Integration Guide
### Step 1: Set Up Your Figma Canvas
- Create a new Figma artboard (e.g., 4000px wide, 2000px tall) to accommodate a horizontal timeline.
- Use a grid (View > Layout Grid) to align elements precisely.

### Step 2: Create the Timeline Structure
- **Draw the Timeline Base**:
  - Use the Line tool (L) to draw a horizontal line across the artboard, representing the 18-month timeline (May 2025 – Nov 2026).
  - Add markers for each month using small vertical lines or circles, labeled with months (e.g., “May 2025,” “Nov 2025,” etc.).
- **Add Phase Nodes**:
  - Create 3 rectangular or circular nodes for each phase (#evaeva_phase1_section, #evaeva_phase2_section, #evaeva_phase3_section).
  - Position them along the timeline:
    - Phase 1: May 2025 – Nov 2025
    - Phase 2: Dec 2025 – May 2026
    - Phase 3: Jun 2026 – Nov 2026
  - Color-code: Phase 1 (blue), Phase 2 (green), Phase 3 (purple).
- **Add Milestone Sub-Nodes**:
  - For each phase, create smaller nodes for milestones (e.g., #phase1_milestone1, #phase1_milestone2, #phase1_milestone3).
  - Connect them to the phase node with arrows (Shift + L for curved arrows).
  - Include sub-nodes for tasks (#m1_tasks, etc.), budget, team, and revenue goals.

### Step 3: Create the End Product Vision
- **Draw the EvaEva AI Hub**:
  - At the right end of the timeline (Nov 2026), create a central circle labeled “EvaEva AI Hub” (#end_product_hub).
  - Use a bold color (e.g., orange) to make it stand out.
- **Add Department Branches**:
  - Draw 9 branches (lines or arrows) extending from the hub to smaller nodes for each department:
    - Sales and Admin AI (#end_sales_admin)
    - Marketing AI (#end_marketing)
    - Content AI (#end_content)
    - Social Media AI (#end_social_media)
    - Advertising AI (#end_advertising)
    - Engineering and Design AI (#end_engineering_design)
    - Finance AI (#end_finance)
    - HR AI (#end_hr)
    - Customer Service AI (#end_customer_service)
  - Use different colors for each department (e.g., Sales: red, Marketing: green, etc.).
- **Add Standalone and Global Nodes**:
  - Create two additional nodes branching from the hub: “Standalone Products” (#end_standalone) and “Global Reach” (#end_global).
  - Connect with arrows to show their role in the end vision.

### Step 4: Populate Text Layers
- **Copy-Paste Text**:
  - Copy the text under each section ID (e.g., #phase1_start, #m1_tasks, #end_sales_admin) from this markdown.
  - Create text layers in Figma (T) and paste the text into the corresponding nodes.
  - Example: Paste “Pre-MVP, solo operation, $80K–$120K budget.” into the #phase1_start node.
- **Format Text**:
  - Use Inter font, 12pt for body text, 16pt for headings (e.g., phase titles).
  - Align text within nodes for clarity (e.g., left-align tasks, center-align milestone titles).

### Step 5: Style and Finalize
- **Apply Colors**:
  - Phases: Blue (Phase 1), Green (Phase 2), Purple (Phase 3).
  - End Product Hub: Orange.
  - Departments: Use a unique color for each (e.g., Sales: red, Marketing: green, Finance: yellow).
- **Add Arrows**:
  - Use the Line tool (L) with arrowheads to show progression between phases and milestones.
  - Example: Arrow from #phase1_start to #phase1_milestone1, then to #phase1_milestone2.
- **Add Labels**:
  - Label the timeline with months (May 2025 – Nov 2026) at the bottom.
  - Add revenue milestones: “$500K” at Nov 2025, “$3M” at May 2026, “$10M” at Nov 2026.
- **Polish**:
  - Group related elements (e.g., Phase 1 node and its milestones) for easy adjustments.
  - Use Figma’s Layout Grid to ensure alignment and spacing.

## Notes for Figma Integration
- **Visual Layout**: The timeline should span 18 months (May 2025 – Nov 2026) with 3 phases, milestones, and an end product hub with department branches.
- **Node Design**: Use rectangles or circles for phases and milestones, circles for the end product hub and departments.
- **Colors**: Blue (Phase 1), Green (Phase 2), Purple (Phase 3), Orange (Hub), varied colors for departments.
- **Text**: Inter font, 12pt for details, 16pt for headings. Keep text concise within nodes.
- **Arrows**: Use curved arrows to connect phases, milestones, and hub branches for a flowchart effect.

### Alternative Solutions for Figma Integration
If manual creation in Figma feels cumbersome, here are alternatives:
1. **Use a Figma Plugin**:
   - Install a plugin like “Text to Figma” or “Markdown to Figma” (if available) to convert markdown to text layers automatically. Search for these in Figma’s Community (Plugins > Browse All Plugins).
2. **Convert to an Image First**:
   - Copy the markdown into a tool like Obsidian or Notion to render it as a structured document.
   - Export as a PDF or PNG, then import the image into Figma (File > Import) and trace over it with shapes and text.
3. **Use FigJam for Brainstorming**:
   - Figma’s companion tool, FigJam, supports importing text to create flowcharts more easily. Paste the markdown into FigJam, convert it to a flowchart, then copy the elements into your Figma canvas.

If you’d prefer a different format (e.g., a table in a text file, or a description of the roadmap as an image I can generate after confirmation), or if you’d like to adjust the timeline further (e.g., 9 months), let me know! You can also provide more details about your Figma setup (e.g., existing design system, preferred colors) to refine the visual instructions.

I’m building *eva_eva* to automate business departments with AI, starting with Sales and Customer Service for real estate, then scaling to a full suite with standalone products. This month-by-month roadmap spans May 2025 to November 2026, hitting $500K by mid-2026 and $10M by late 2026. <xaiArtifact artifact_id="31cb2289-c727-4981-a7e9-2f0efe8fb518" artifact_version_id="b173d4d4-74c2-4043-8aa8-451a993c16e3" title="EvaEva Month-by-Month Roadmap Figma Output" contentType="text/markdown">

# EvaEva Month-by-Month Roadmap Figma Output

This roadmap details my 18-month journey from pre-MVP to a full-suite AI platform, broken down by month from May 2025 to November 2026. It targets $500K by mid-2026 and $10M by late 2026, formatted for Figma with section IDs for a visual timeline.

## Phase 1: MVP Development and Launch (May 2025 – Nov 2025)
###evaeva_phase1_section
- **May 2025: Kickoff and Planning** (#month_may_2025)
  - Finalize $80K–$120K budget, secure outsourcing.
  - Outsource 2 developers ($5K/month each), 1 UI/UX designer ($3K/month).
  - Set up tech stack: Node.js, MongoDB, Twilio.
- **Jun 2025: Sales AI Development** (#month_jun_2025)
  - Build Sales AI: Lead qualification (“not interested,” “call back later”), Vapi integration ($0.05/call).
  - Develop analytics: Cost-per-meeting, calls made, meetings booked.
  - Budget: $20K (dev tools, API costs).
- **Jul 2025: Customer AI Development** (#month_jul_2025)
  - Build Customer AI: Inquiry automation (80% coverage), multi-language (English, Arabic).
  - Analytics: Average call time, answered calls, cost per day.
  - Budget: $20K.
- **Aug 2025: Finalize MVP Features** (#month_aug_2025)
  - Add segmentation: “Not interested,” “call back later,” “no answer” sections.
  - Integrate dashboard: Calls/day, meetings booked, off-plan vs. secondary properties.
  - Budget: $20K.
- **Sep 2025: Alpha Testing** (#month_sep_2025)
  - Test with 5 Dubai agencies (e.g., Better Homes).
  - Measure: 50% lead task automation, 20-hour/week savings.
  - Budget: $10K (incentives, tools).
- **Oct 2025: Refine and Prepare Launch** (#month_oct_2025)
  - Refine AI based on feedback (e.g., “Sophie” with Dubai slang).
  - Hire 1 QA engineer ($3K/month).
  - Prep marketing: LinkedIn ads, 14-day trials.
- **Nov 2025: MVP Launch** (#month_nov_2025)
  - Launch Sales and Customer AI: Starter Plan ($99/month).
  - Target: 210 customers (150 small agencies, 50 mid-sized, 10 enterprises).
  - Revenue: $500K (150 at $1,188/year, 50 at $3,588/year, 10 at $12,000/year).
  - Budget: $65K marketing.

## Phase 2: Rapid Expansion and Multi-Agent Rollout (Dec 2025 – May 2026)
###evaeva_phase2_section
- **Dec 2025: Marketing AI Development** (#month_dec_2025)
  - Build Marketing AI: Campaign automation, ROI tracking.
  - Integrate with Mailchimp, Salesforce.
  - Budget: $30K.
- **Jan 2026: Marketing AI Launch** (#month_jan_2026)
  - Launch Pro Plan ($299/month).
  - Marketing: Google Ads, webinars.
  - Target: 400 small agencies, 150 mid-sized firms.
- **Feb 2026: Content AI Development** (#month_feb_2026)
  - Build Content AI: Listings, blogs, emails.
  - Test with 10 mid-sized firms (e.g., Coldwell Banker).
  - Budget: $20K.
- **Mar 2026: Social Media AI Development** (#month_mar_2026)
  - Build Social Media AI: Post automation, engagement tracking.
  - Test with 5 firms, integrate LinkedIn, Twitter APIs.
  - Budget: $20K.
- **Apr 2026: Content and Social Media AI Launch** (#month_apr_2026)
  - Launch Content/Social Media AI as add-ons ($49/month each).
  - Marketing: MIPIM demos, 20% annual discounts.
  - Target: 800 customers (400 small, 300 mid-sized, 100 enterprises).
- **May 2026: Scale Operations** (#month_may_2026)
  - Expand to UK, Singapore: Localize AI.
  - Revenue: $3M (400 at $2,000/year, 300 at $5,000/year, 100 at $12,000/year).
  - Budget: $70K/month marketing.
  - Hire 1 sales lead ($6K/month).

## Phase 3: Full Suite and Standalone Products (Jun 2026 – Nov 2026)
###evaeva_phase3_section
- **Jun 2026: Advertising AI Development** (#month_jun_2026)
  - Build Advertising AI: Ad creation, budget optimization.
  - Test with 10 enterprises (e.g., Emaar).
  - Budget: $20K.
- **Jul 2026: Engineering/Design AI Development** (#month_jul_2026)

### Roadmap 2: Week-by-Week Breakdown

EvaEva Week-by-Week Roadmap
This roadmap details my 18-month journey from pre-MVP to a full-suite AI platform, broken down by week from May 2025 to November 2026. It targets $500K by mid-2026 and $10M by late 2026.

Phase 1: MVP Development and Launch (May 2025 – Nov 2025, 26 Weeks)
Week 1 (May 5–11, 2025): Kickoff and Planning
- Finalize $80K–$120K budget, secure outsourcing.
- Outsource 2 developers ($5K/month each), 1 UI/UX designer ($3K/month).
- Set up tech stack: Node.js, MongoDB, Twilio.
Week 2–3 (May 12–25, 2025): Project Setup
- Define requirements for Sales and Customer AI.
- Configure development environment, API keys (Vapi, Twilio).
Week 4 (May 26–Jun 1, 2025): Sales AI Design
- Design lead qualification flow (“not interested,” “call back later”).
- Plan analytics dashboard (cost-per-meeting).
Week 5–7 (Jun 2–22, 2025): Sales AI Development
- Code Sales AI with Vapi integration ($0.05/call).
- Implement analytics: Calls made, meetings booked.
- Budget: $15K.
Week 8–10 (Jun 23–Jul 13, 2025): Customer AI Development
- Code Customer AI: Inquiry automation (80% coverage).
- Add multi-language support (English, Arabic).
- Analytics: Average call time, cost per day.
- Budget: $15K.
Week 11–13 (Jul 14–Aug 3, 2025): MVP Feature Integration
- Add segmentation: “Not interested,” “call back later,” “no answer.”
- Build dashboard: Calls/day, off-plan vs. secondary properties.
- Budget: $15K.
Week 14–16 (Aug 4–24, 2025): Testing Prep
- Prepare test cases for 5 Dubai agencies.
- Set up testing tools, incentive plans.
Week 17–19 (Aug 25–Sep 14, 2025): Alpha Testing
- Test with 5 Dubai agencies (e.g., Better Homes).
- Measure: 50% lead task automation, 20-hour/week savings.
- Budget: $10K.
Week 20–22 (Sep 15–Oct 5, 2025): Refinement
- Refine AI based on feedback (e.g., “Sophie” with Dubai slang).

### Integration Notes for FigJam
- **Paste and Organize**: Copy the entire text into a FigJam board. Use FigJam’s text tool to paste each section (e.g., “May 2025: Kickoff and Planning” or “Week 1 (May 5–11, 2025): Kickoff and Planning”) into sticky notes or text boxes.
- **Visual Design**:
  - Use FigJam’s shapes (circles, rectangles) to create a timeline. Draw a horizontal line and place weekly/monthly nodes along it.
  - Color-code phases (blue for Phase 1, green for Phase 2, purple for Phase 3) using FigJam’s fill tool.
  - Add arrows or connectors between milestones (e.g., from “Alpha Testing” to “MVP Launch”) to show progression.
  - Use icons (available in FigJam’s stamp tool) like a gear for development or dollar sign for revenue goals.
- **End Product Visualization**: At the end of the timeline (November 2026), create a central circle labeled “EvaEva AI Hub” with lines branching out to text boxes for each department (Sales and Admin, Marketing, etc.).
- **Appeal**: Space out elements evenly, use bold headings for months/weeks, and highlight key milestones (e.g., launches, revenue targets) in larger text or different colors.
- **Export to Figma**: Once styled in FigJam, export the board as an image (File > Export) or copy elements to Figma if needed for your design system.

These roadmaps are detailed, covering every task, budget, team change, and revenue milestone, making them ready for a visually stunning FigJam layout. If you need adjustments (e.g., shorter timeline, specific tasks added), let me know!

### Roadmap 1: Month-by-Month Breakdown

EvaEva Month-by-Month Roadmap
This roadmap details my 18-month journey from pre-MVP to a full-suite AI platform, broken down by month from May 2025 to November 2026. It targets $500K by mid-2026 and $10M by late 2026.

Phase 1: MVP Development and Launch (May 2025 – Nov 2025)
May 2025: Kickoff and Planning
1. Finalize $80K–$120K budget, secure outsourcing.
2. Outsource 2 developers ($5K/month each), 1 UI/UX designer ($3K/month).
3. Set up tech stack: Node.js, MongoDB, Twilio.
Jun 2025: Sales AI Development
1. Build Sales AI: Lead qualification (“not interested,” “call back later”), Vapi integration ($0.05/call).
2. Develop analytics: Cost-per-meeting, calls made, meetings booked.
3. Budget: $20K (dev tools, API costs).
Jul 2025: Customer AI Development
1. Build Customer AI: Inquiry automation (80% coverage), multi-language (English, Arabic).
2. Analytics: Average call time, answered calls, cost per day.
3. Budget: $20K.
Aug 2025: Finalize MVP Features
1. Add segmentation: “Not interested,” “call back later,” “no answer” sections.
2. Integrate dashboard: Calls/day, meetings booked, off-plan vs. secondary properties.
3. Budget: $20K.
Sep 2025: Alpha Testing
1. Test with 5 Dubai agencies (e.g., Better Homes).
2. Measure: 50% lead task automation, 20-hour/week savings.
3. Budget: $10K (incentives, tools).
Oct 2025: Refine and Prepare Launch
1. Refine AI based on feedback (e.g., “Sophie” with Dubai slang).
2. Hire 1 QA engineer ($3K/month).
3. Prep marketing: LinkedIn ads, 14-day trials.
Nov 2025: MVP Launch
1. Launch Sales and Customer AI: Starter Plan ($99/month).
2. Target: 210 customers (150 small agencies, 50 mid-sized, 10 enterprises).
3. Revenue: $500K (150 at $1,188/year, 50 at $3,588/year, 10 at $12,000/year).
4. Budget: $65K marketing.
5. Hire 1 marketing lead ($5K/month), 1 customer support ($3K/month).

Phase 2: Rapid Expansion and Multi-Agent Rollout (Dec 2025 – May 2026)
Dec 2025: Marketing AI Development
1. Build Marketing AI: Campaign automation, ROI tracking.
2. Integrate with Mailchimp, Salesforce.
3. Budget: $30K.
Jan 2026: Marketing AI Launch
1. Launch Pro Plan ($299/month).
2. Marketing: Google Ads, webinars.
3. Target: 400 small agencies, 150 mid-sized firms.
Feb 2026: Content AI Development
1. Build Content AI: Listings, blogs, emails.
2. Test with 10 mid-sized firms (e.g., Coldwell Banker).
3. Budget: $20K.
Mar 2026: Social Media AI Development
1. Build Social Media AI: Post automation, engagement tracking.
2. Test with 5 firms, integrate LinkedIn, Twitter APIs.
3. Budget: $20K.
Apr 2026: Content and Social Media AI Launch
1. Launch Content/Social Media AI as add-ons ($49/month each).
2. Marketing: MIPIM demos, 20% annual discounts.
3. Target: 800 customers (400 small, 300 mid-sized, 100 enterprises).
May 2026: Scale Operations
1. Expand to UK, Singapore: Localize AI.
2. Revenue: $3M (400 at $2,000/year, 300 at $5,000/year, 100 at $12,000/year).
3. Budget: $70K/month marketing.
4. Hire 1 sales lead ($6K/month).

Phase 3: Full Suite and Standalone Products (Jun 2026 – Nov 2026)
Jun 2026: Advertising AI Development
1. Build Advertising AI: Ad creation, budget optimization.
2. Test with 10 enterprises (e.g., Emaar).
3. Budget: $20K.
Jul 2026: Engineering/Design AI Development
1. Build Engineering/Design AI: Floor plans, 3D renderings.
2. Test with 10 enterprises.
3. Budget: $20K.
Aug 2026: Finance AI Development
1. Build Finance AI: Budget tracking, forecasting.
2. Test with 10 enterprises (e.g., JLL).
3. Budget: $20K.
Sep 2026: HR AI Development
1. Build HR AI: Recruitment, onboarding.
2. Test with 10 enterprises.
3. Budget: $20K.
Oct 2026: Full Suite Integration
1. Integrate Advertising, Engineering/Design, Finance, HR AI.
2. Test with 20 enterprises (e.g., Emaar, Hilton).
3. Budget: $10K.
Nov 2026: Full Suite and Standalone Launch
1. Launch Enterprise Plan ($1,000+/month): Full suite.
2. Offer standalone products: Sales AI ($99/month), Marketing AI ($149/month), etc.
3. Marketing: PR Newswire, World Economic Forum, global expansion (China, India).
4. Target: 2,500 customers (1,000 small, 1,000 mid-sized, 500 enterprises).
5. Revenue: $10M (1,000 at $2,000/year, 1,000 at $5,000/year, 500 at $15,000/year).
6. Budget: $80K/month marketing.
7. Hire 1 product manager ($7K/month), 1 global lead ($8K/month).

End Product Vision (Nov 2026)

  - Sales and Admin AI: Lead qualification, admin automation.

- Global Reach: 2,500 customers across Dubai, US, UK, Singapore, China, India.

- Revenue: $10M, 70–80% SaaS margins, 5–10x ROI for investors.

FigJam Integration Tips
- Paste this text into a FigJam board.
- Use sticky notes or text boxes for each numbered task under each week.
- Draw a horizontal timeline with lines or arrows connecting weeks.
- Color-code phases: Phase 1 (blue), Phase 2 (green), Phase 3 (purple).
- Use circles for milestones (e.g., launches, revenue checks), add icons (e.g., dollar signs).
- Create a central “EvaEva AI Hub” node at the end with branches for departments.

---

### How to Import into FigJam

1. **Open FigJam**: Start a new FigJam board in your Figma workspace.
2. **Paste the Text**: Copy the entire text of either roadmap (month-by-month or week-by-week) and paste it into the FigJam canvas. FigJam will place the text as a single block.
3. **Separate Tasks**:
   - Click the text block and use FigJam’s “Break Text” feature (right-click > Break Text) or manually select and drag each numbered line into a new sticky note or text box.
   - Alternatively, after pasting, press “Enter” after each numbered task to create new lines, then convert each line into a sticky note (select line, press Ctrl+Shift+N or Cmd+Shift+N).
4. **Create the Timeline**:
   - Use FigJam’s line tool to draw a horizontal timeline.
   - Place sticky notes for each month or week along the line, grouping tasks under their respective periods.
5. **Visual Appeal**:
   - Color-code phases (blue for Phase 1, green for Phase 2, purple for Phase 3) using the fill color tool.
   - Add circles or shapes for milestones (e.g., “MVP Launch,” “Revenue: $10M”) and use icons from the stamp tool (e.g., dollar sign, gear).
   - Draw arrows between milestones to show progression.
6. **End Product Visualization**:
   - At the end (November 2026), create a central circle labeled “EvaEva AI Hub” and add branches with text boxes for each department (Sales and Admin, Marketing, etc.).
7. **Adjust Layout**: Space out elements evenly, use bold text for headings (e.g., months, weeks), and align tasks neatly for a clean look.

This revised format with numbered tasks should ensure FigJam imports all stages, not just the first and last. If you still face issues, try pasting smaller sections at a time or let me know, and I can adjust further (e.g., single-line entries per task).

End Product Vision (Nov 2026)  
- EvaEva AI Hub: Central platform with modular AI agents.  
  - Sales and Admin AI: Lead qualification, admin automation.  
  - Marketing AI: Campaign automation, ROI tracking.  
  - Content AI: Listings, blogs, emails.

  - Engineering and Design AI: Floor plans, 3D renderings.  
  - Finance AI: Budgeting, forecasting.  
  - HR AI: Recruitment, onboarding.  
  - Customer Service AI: Inquiry automation, support ticketing.

- Compliance: GDPR, CCPA, UAE laws.  
- Revenue: $10M, 70–80% SaaS margins, 5–10x ROI for investors.  

FigJam Integration Tips  
- Paste this text into a FigJam board.  
- Use sticky notes or text boxes for each numbered task under each week.  
- Draw a horizontal timeline with lines or arrows connecting weeks.  
- Color-code phases: Phase 1 (blue), Phase 2 (green), Phase 3 (purple).  
- Use circles for milestones (e.g., launches, revenue checks), add icons (e.g., dollar signs).  
- Create a central “EvaEva AI Hub” node at the end with branches for departments.  

---

### How to Import into FigJam

1. **Open FigJam**: Start a new FigJam board.
2. **Paste the Text**: Copy the entire text above and paste it into the FigJam canvas. It will appear as a single block.
3. **Separate Tasks**:
   - Select the text block, right-click, and choose “Break Text” to split it into individual lines, or press “Enter” after each numbered task.
   - Convert each numbered line into a sticky note (select line, press Ctrl+Shift+N or Cmd+Shift+N).
4. **Create the Timeline**:
   - Use the line tool to draw a horizontal timeline spanning May 12, 2025, to November 8, 2026.
   - Place sticky notes for each week along the timeline, grouping tasks under their respective weeks.
5. **Visual Appeal**:
   - Color-code phases (blue for Phase 1, green for Phase 2, purple for Phase 3).
   - Use circles or shapes for milestones (e.g., “MVP Launch,” “Revenue: $10M”) and add icons (e.g., dollar sign, gear).
   - Draw arrows between weeks to show progression.
6. **End Product Visualization**:
   - At the end (November 2026), create a central circle labeled “EvaEva AI Hub” with branches (lines) to text boxes for each department (Sales and Admin, Marketing, etc.).

- **Task Granularity**: Each week includes 1–5 tasks, ensuring all milestones (e.g., development, testing, launches) are captured, addressing the prior issue of missing intermediate tasks.
- **FigJam Fix**: Numbered tasks on separate lines should ensure FigJam imports each as a distinct element, not just the first and last.
- **Alignment**: Matches the prior month-by-month roadmap but with finer granularity, maintaining the same phases, milestones, and goals.

If you still encounter issues with FigJam imports (e.g., tasks not separating), try pasting smaller sections (e.g., one phase at a time) or let me know, and I can adjust further!

|----------------|---------------------|---------------------|---------------------|-------------------------|------------------|------------------|---------------------|---------------|
| **Best Case**  | 109,000            | 83,000             | 762,000            | 530,000                | 174,000          | 954,000          | 500K (Nov 25), 3M (May 26), 10M (Nov 26) | 2,546,000     |

### Explanation of the Table
- **Columns**:
  - **Scenario**: Best Case, Moderate, Minimal (descending budget levels).
  - **Phase 1 Cost**: Costs to complete Sales and Customer Service AI (development + other expenses).
  - **Phase 2 Cost**: Costs to develop Marketing and Content AI.
  - **Phase 3 Cost**: Costs for going to market, including development, marketing, and staff.
  - **Marketing Budget**: Specific marketing expenses within Phase 3.
  - **Staff Cost**: Total staff-related expenses across all phases.
  - **Total Cost**: Sum of all costs.
  - **Revenue**: Projected revenue at key milestones (November 2025, mid-2026, November 2026).
  - **Surplus**: Remaining funds after costs (Total Revenue - Total Cost).

- **Row Details**:
  - **Best Case ($954K)**: Full outsourcing, aggressive marketing ($530K), 6 staff, on-schedule 78 weeks.
  - **Moderate ($448K)**: Reduced outsourcing (1 developer/phase), lean marketing ($170K), 4 staff, slight delays.
  - **Minimal ($192K)**: Solo-driven, minimal marketing ($70K), 3 staff, extended timelines.

- **Financing Notes**: Assumes $50K–$120K initial funding, with revenue reinvestment covering subsequent phases. Surpluses range from $2.546M (Best) to $2.808M (Minimal).

### How to Insert into a Financing Table
1. **Copy the Table**: Copy the text above into a text editor or spreadsheet (e.g., Excel, Google Sheets).
2. **Format in Spreadsheet**:
   - Paste into a new sheet.
   - Adjust column widths to fit content.
   - Use borders to define cells (select all, Format > Borders).
   - Add currency formatting to cost columns (e.g., $###,###).
3. **Import into Document**: Copy the formatted table into your financing document (e.g., Word, PDF) or directly into Figma/FigJam as a text box or image.
4. **Visual Enhancement** (optional):
   - In Figma/FigJam, use the table as a text layer, then add colors (e.g., green for surplus) or icons (e.g., dollar sign) for visual appeal.
   - Export as an image from the spreadsheet if needed for Figma import.

This table provides a clear financial overview for your stakeholders or investors, matching the roadmap’s milestones.

   - Adjust prompts (e.g., add “more detailed” or “brighter lights”) if needed.
5. **Insert into Presentation**:
   - Download the image and import it into Figma/FigJam or a PowerPoint slide for your investor pitch.

### **ASSISTANT**:
To provide a detailed infrastructure example of the server that would support your fully completed *eva_eva* AI platform by November 8, 2026, I’ll outline a robust, scalable server architecture based on the project’s requirements from our discussions. This server will handle the AI agents (Sales and Admin, Marketing, Content, Social Media, Advertising, Engineering and Design, Finance, HR, and Customer Service), real-time analytics (e.g., cost-per-meeting, calls/day, off-plan vs. secondary), and global reach (Dubai, US, UK, Singapore, China, India), targeting $10M revenue. The infrastructure will leverage the tech stack (Node.js, MongoDB, Twilio, Vapi APIs) and ensure compliance (GDPR, CCPA, UAE laws). I’ll also include relevant icons you can add to your Figma presentation to visually represent each component for your investor.

### Detailed Server Infrastructure Example

The server infrastructure will consist of a cloud-based, multi-tier architecture hosted on a major provider like Amazon Web Services (AWS) or Google Cloud Platform (GCP), optimized for scalability and performance. Here’s the breakdown:

1. **Load Balancer Tier**  
   - **Purpose**: Distributes incoming traffic across multiple application servers to ensure high availability and fault tolerance.  
   - **Technology**: AWS Elastic Load Balancer (ELB) or GCP Load Balancer.  
   - **Capacity**: Handles 10,000+ concurrent users by November 2026, supporting 2,500 customers.  

2. **Application Tier**  
   - **Web Servers**:  
     - **Quantity**: 4 virtual machines (e.g., AWS EC2 t3.large instances or GCP Compute Engine n2-standard-4).  
     - **Specs**: 2 vCPUs, 8 GB RAM each, running Node.js for API endpoints (e.g., Vapi call handling, Twilio integration).  
     - **Configuration**: Auto-scaling group to add instances during peak loads (e.g., real estate season in Dubai).  
   - **AI Processing Servers**:  
     - **Quantity**: 2 dedicated instances (e.g., AWS EC2 g4dn.xlarge with GPU support).  
     - **Specs**: 4 vCPUs, 16 GB RAM, NVIDIA T4 GPU for AI model inference (e.g., lead qualification, content generation).  

3. **Database Tier**  
   - **Primary Database**: MongoDB Atlas cluster (M30 tier).  
     - **Specs**: 2 replica sets, 8 GB RAM, 40 GB storage, sharded for scalability across regions (Dubai, US, Singapore).  
     - **Data**: Stores user profiles, analytics, AI training data, and multi-language content (English, Arabic).  
   - **Caching Layer**: Redis instance (AWS ElastiCache or GCP Memorystore).  
     - **Specs**: 1 node, 2 GB RAM, for caching frequent queries (e.g., dashboard analytics).  

4. **Storage Tier**  
   - **Object Storage**: AWS S3 or GCP Cloud Storage.  
     - **Capacity**: 500 GB, storing AI-generated assets (e.g., 3D renderings, ad creatives), with lifecycle policies for cost efficiency.  
   - **Backup**: Daily snapshots to a secondary region, encrypted for compliance.  

5. **Networking and Security**  
   - **CDN**: AWS CloudFront or GCP CDN for global content delivery (low latency in China, India).  
   - **Firewall**: AWS Security Groups or GCP Firewall Rules, restricting access to authorized IPs.  
   - **Security**: SSL/TLS encryption, biometric-authenticated access to physical servers, and compliance monitoring for GDPR, CCPA, UAE laws.  

6. **Monitoring and Management**  
   - **Tool**: AWS CloudWatch or GCP Stackdriver.  
     - **Metrics**: CPU usage, API response time, database latency, tracked 24/7.  
   - **Alerting**: Email/SMS notifications for downtime or performance thresholds.  

### Estimated Specifications
- **Total Servers**: 6 (4 web, 2 AI processing).  
- **Storage**: 540 GB (40 GB MongoDB + 500 GB S3).  
- **Bandwidth**: 1 TB/month, scalable to 5 TB with growth.  
- **Cost**: ~$1,500/month (initial), scaling to $5,000/month by 2026 with revenue reinvestment.

- **Load Balancer**: "load-balancer" or "network-switch" (e.g., FontAwesome "fas fa-exchange-alt").  
- **Web Server**: "server" or "web-hosting" (e.g., Material Icons "server").  
- **AI Processing Server**: "neural-network" or "ai" (e.g., Flaticon "artificial-intelligence").  
- **Database**: "database" or "storage" (e.g., FontAwesome "fas fa-database").  
- **Caching Layer**: "memory" or "cache" (e.g., Material Icons "memory").  
- **Object Storage**: "cloud-storage" or "s3" (e.g., Flaticon "cloud-upload").  
- **CDN**: "globe" or "cdn" (e.g., FontAwesome "fas fa-globe").

This infrastructure ensures your platform can handle the projected growth, impressing your investor with its robustness and forward-thinking design.

- Research suggests checking the website's HTML, CSS, and JavaScript for mobile compatibility could help resolve the issue.

### Direct Answer

#### Understanding the Issue
Your website, [invalid url, do not cite], has a services section where clicking on categories like "aesthetics" and "training services" should take users to specific sections on the page, but this doesn't work on mobile devices. This is likely due to how the website handles navigation on smaller screens, possibly related to anchor links or responsive design.

#### Steps to Fix the Problem
Here are some simple steps to troubleshoot and fix the issue:

- **Check the Viewport Tag**: Ensure your website has a meta viewport tag in the HTML head, like `<meta name="viewport" content="width=device-width, initial-scale=1.0">`, to make sure it scales properly on mobile devices.
- **Verify Anchor Links**: Make sure each section (e.g., "aesthetics") has a unique ID, and the navigation links point to these IDs correctly, such as `<a href="#aesthetics">Aesthetics</a>`.
- **Inspect CSS for Mobile**: Use your browser's developer tools to simulate a mobile device and check if any CSS rules are hiding or misaligning the sections on mobile.
- **Review JavaScript**: If navigation uses JavaScript (like smooth scrolling), ensure it works on mobile browsers by checking for errors in the developer tools.
- **Test on Different Devices**: Try viewing the website on various mobile devices and browsers (e.g., Safari, Chrome) to see if the issue is specific to one device or browser.

#### Next Steps
If you're not familiar with web development, consider consulting a web developer to inspect the code and fix the issue. Testing on tools like [BrowserStack](https://www.browserstack.com/) can also help simulate different mobile environments.

### Survey Note: Detailed Analysis of Mobile Navigation Issues on Your Website

This section provides a comprehensive analysis of the mobile navigation issue on your website, [invalid url, do not cite], where clicking on "aesthetics" and "training services" in the services section does not navigate to the respective sections on mobile devices, unlike other categories. The analysis is based on common web development practices and potential issues identified through research into mobile-friendly navigation.

#### Background and Problem Description
Your website includes a services section with categories such as "hair," "aesthetics," "non-surgical," "beauty treatments," and "training services." On desktop, clicking these categories likely uses anchor links to jump to specific sections on the same page, providing a seamless user experience. However, on mobile devices, this functionality fails for "aesthetics" and "training services," suggesting a mobile-specific issue with navigation.

Given the current date, Thursday, April 24, 2025, at 06:09 PM +04, the issue is likely related to modern web development practices and mobile browser behavior. The analysis below outlines potential causes and detailed steps to resolve the problem, drawing from research into common mobile navigation issues.

#### Potential Causes and Detailed Troubleshooting Steps

1. **Responsive Design and Viewport Configuration**
   - **Issue**: Mobile devices require websites to be responsive, scaling content to fit different screen sizes. If the viewport is not configured correctly, navigation elements may not function as expected.
   - **Solution**: Ensure your website includes a meta viewport tag in the HTML head section, such as:
     ```html
     <meta name="viewport" content="width=device-width, initial-scale=1.0">
     ```
     This tag ensures the website adapts to mobile screens, preventing scaling issues that could affect anchor links.
   - **Research Insight**: According to [Mobile-Friendly Navigation Best Practices](https://www.bruceclay.com/blog/mobile-friendly-navigation/), proper viewport configuration is essential for mobile usability, ensuring elements like navigation menus are accessible.

2. **Anchor Link Implementation**
   - **Issue**: Anchor links (e.g., `<a href="#aesthetics">Aesthetics</a>`) rely on unique IDs in the HTML (e.g., `<div id="aesthetics">...</div>`) to navigate to sections. On mobile, these links may fail if the IDs are missing, misnamed, or if the content is dynamically loaded.
   - **Solution**: Verify that each section has a unique ID and that navigation links point to these IDs correctly. For example:
     - Section: `<div id="aesthetics">Aesthetics Content</div>`
     - Link: `<a href="#aesthetics">Aesthetics</a>`
   - If the website uses JavaScript for smooth scrolling, ensure the script is compatible with mobile browsers. Check for errors in the browser's developer tools (e.g., Chrome DevTools) while simulating a mobile device.
   - **Research Insight**: [Mobile Navigation Patterns and Examples](https://www.justinmind.com/blog/mobile-navigation/) highlights that anchor links are common for single-page navigation, but mobile-specific CSS or JavaScript can disrupt their functionality.

3. **CSS and Media Queries for Mobile**
   - **Issue**: CSS rules, especially media queries for mobile screens (e.g., `@media (max-width: 768px)`), may hide or reposition sections, preventing anchor links from working. Touch-friendly design is also crucial, as mobile users rely on taps rather than clicks.
   - **Solution**: Use developer tools to simulate a mobile device and inspect the CSS applied to navigation and sections. Look for rules that might:
     - Hide sections (e.g., `display: none`).
     - Alter layout (e.g., `position: absolute` or `overflow: hidden`).
     - Ensure navigation elements have large enough tap targets (e.g., minimum 48x48 pixels, as per [Common Reasons Websites Don’t Work on Mobile](https://www.makeuseof.com/mobile-responsive-reasons-your-website-isnt/)).
   - Adjust media queries to ensure sections remain visible and accessible on mobile.
   - **Research Insight**: [9 Reasons Why Your Website Doesn't Work On Mobile Devices](https://www.vertical-leap.uk/blog/9-reasons-website-doesnt-work-mobile/) notes that improper CSS scaling can lead to navigation issues, especially with headers and menus.

4. **JavaScript and Dynamic Content**
   - **Issue**: If your website is a single-page application (SPA) or uses frameworks like React, Vue, or Angular, content may load dynamically. Anchor links may fail if the target section is not yet rendered when clicked, particularly on mobile due to performance differences.
   - **Solution**: Ensure JavaScript handles navigation correctly on mobile. Check for console errors in developer tools and verify that sections are fully loaded before navigation links are clicked. If using smooth scrolling libraries, ensure they are mobile-compatible.
   - Consider delaying navigation until content is loaded, using event listeners like `DOMContentLoaded` or `load`.
   - **Research Insight**: [6 Common Mobile Website Issues and Solutions](https://www.hotjar.com/website-problems/mobile/) suggests that dynamic content loading can cause navigation issues, especially on mobile, due to slower JavaScript execution.

5. **Testing Across Devices and Browsers**
   - **Issue**: The problem may be device- or browser-specific, affecting certain mobile devices (e.g., iPhones, Android phones) or browsers (e.g., Safari, Chrome, Firefox).
   - **Solution**: Test your website on various mobile devices and browsers to identify patterns. Use online tools like [BrowserStack](https://www.browserstack.com/) to simulate different environments without physical devices.
   - Pay attention to touch interactions, as mobile navigation relies on taps, which may differ from desktop clicks.
   - **Research Insight**: [The most common (and egregious) mobile nav problem](https://uxwest.com/the-most-common-and-egregious-mobile-nav-problem/) emphasizes testing across devices to ensure intuitive navigation, especially for touch-based interactions.

#### Comparative Analysis of Navigation Issues

To organize the potential causes and solutions, the following table summarizes the key areas to investigate:

| **Area**               | **Potential Issue**                              | **Solution**                                                                 |
|------------------------|--------------------------------------------------|-----------------------------------------------------------------------------|
| Viewport Configuration | Incorrect scaling on mobile                      | Add `<meta name="viewport" content="width=device-width, initial-scale=1.0">` |
| Anchor Links           | Missing or misnamed IDs, dynamic content loading | Verify IDs and ensure sections are loaded before navigation                 |
| CSS and Media Queries  | Hidden sections, small tap targets               | Adjust media queries, ensure touch-friendly design                          |
| JavaScript             | Incompatible scripts, console errors             | Check for errors, ensure mobile compatibility                               |
| Device/Browser Testing | Device-specific failures                         | Test on multiple devices and browsers, use [BrowserStack](https://www.browserstack.com/) |

#### Additional Considerations
- If the website uses a hamburger menu for mobile navigation, ensure it is intuitive and accessible, as per [Mobile navigation: patterns and examples](https://www.justinmind.com/blog/mobile-navigation/).
- Consider accessibility, ensuring navigation works with screen readers and assistive technologies, which is crucial for mobile users.
- If the issue persists, consult a web developer to inspect the code directly, as manual inspection may reveal framework-specific problems (e.g., React Router, Vue Router).

#### Conclusion
The mobile navigation issue on your website likely stems from anchor link implementation, CSS media queries, or JavaScript compatibility on mobile devices. By following the troubleshooting steps outlined—checking the viewport, verifying anchor links, inspecting CSS, reviewing JavaScript, and testing across devices—you should be able to identify and resolve the problem. If you're not familiar with web development, seeking professional assistance is recommended to ensure a smooth user experience.

### Key Citations
- [Mobile-Friendly Navigation Best Practices](https://www.bruceclay.com/blog/mobile-friendly-navigation/)
- [Mobile Navigation Patterns and Examples](https://www.justinmind.com/blog/mobile-navigation/)
- [9 Reasons Why Your Website Doesn't Work On Mobile Devices](https://www.vertical-leap.uk/blog/9-reasons-website-doesnt-work-mobile/)

### Survey Note: Detailed Analysis and Recommendations for Website Scrolling Issues

This section provides a comprehensive analysis of the issues reported with your website, particularly the admin section's scrolling and component display problems on mobile devices, such as your Samsung device. The focus is on identifying potential causes and offering detailed troubleshooting steps, drawing from common web development practices and research findings.

#### Background and Problem Description
You have encountered issues with the admin login section of your website, [transformedacademyhq.co.uk](https://transformedacademyhq.co.uk), where navigation is impaired, and scrolling does not work, especially in mobile view. Login details provided are drivendatadynamics@gmail.com with password DCLrip7292!. The problem has worsened after interventions by a VS Code augmented AI agent, which initially claimed to fix the issue but instead exacerbated it. Components are also not displaying properly on the screen, particularly on mobile devices.

Given the complexity, the analysis begins by considering common causes for mobile scrolling issues, informed by web development resources and best practices. The goal is to guide you through a systematic approach to diagnose and resolve the problem, acknowledging that without direct access to the code (stored privately on GitHub), general troubleshooting is necessary.

#### Potential Causes and Detailed Troubleshooting Steps

##### 1. Browser and Device-Specific Issues
Research suggests that scrolling problems can sometimes stem from browser-specific issues, such as cache conflicts or extensions. For instance, restarting the browser or clearing cookies and caches might resolve temporary glitches, as noted in [Why A Website Won't Scroll & How to Fix it](https://alyamanalhayekdesign.com/blog/my-website-wont-scroll/). Given your use of a Samsung device, ensure the browser (likely Chrome or Samsung Internet) is updated and test on another mobile browser to isolate device-specific issues.

##### 2. CSS-Related Causes
One of the most common reasons for scrolling not working on mobile is CSS settings, particularly the `overflow` property. If `overflow: hidden` is applied to the body, main container, or a parent element in the admin section, it will prevent scrolling. This is supported by findings from [Stack Overflow: I cannot scroll down on any page of my website using Android devices](https://stackoverflow.com/questions/64355752/i-cannot-scroll-down-on-any-page-of-my-website-using-android-devices), where a similar issue was resolved by changing `main {overflow: hidden;}` to allow scrolling.

To investigate:
- Use your browser's developer tools to simulate mobile view (e.g., Chrome DevTools' device toolbar).
- Log into the admin section and inspect the computed styles for the body and container elements. Look for `overflow: hidden` and consider changing it to `auto` or `scroll` if possible.
- Check media queries for mobile-specific CSS rules that might inadvertently disable scrolling.

Additionally, ensure the viewport meta tag is correctly set, such as `<meta name="viewport" content="width=device-width, initial-scale=1.0">`, to ensure proper mobile rendering. Incorrect viewport settings can lead to layout issues, affecting component visibility.

##### 3. JavaScript Interference
JavaScript can also interfere with scrolling, especially on mobile devices where touch events are critical. Scripts that call `preventDefault()` on touchstart or touchmove events can block default scrolling behavior. For example, libraries handling modals or overlays might lock scrolling, which could be relevant if the admin section uses such features.

To check:
- Open the developer tools and navigate to the "Event Listeners" tab to see if there are touch or scroll event handlers attached to elements, particularly in the admin section.
- Temporarily disable JavaScript (via browser settings or DevTools) to see if scrolling works without it. If it does, the issue is likely JavaScript-related.
- Review the console for errors, as JavaScript failures can disrupt scrolling functionality.

##### 4. Layout and Component Display Issues
You mentioned that components are not showing properly, which could contribute to the perception that scrolling doesn't work. This might occur if elements are positioned off-screen, have incorrect dimensions, or are hidden due to CSS properties like `display: none` or `visibility: hidden`.

To address:
- Inspect the layout in mobile view to ensure all components are within the viewport. Check for elements with `position: fixed` or `position: absolute` that might cover scrollable areas or push content out of view.
- Verify that the content height exceeds the viewport height, as without overflow, there would be nothing to scroll. This can be checked by inspecting the computed height of containers in DevTools.
- Ensure proper nesting of HTML elements, as malformed structure can lead to rendering issues, though this is less likely the primary cause.

##### 5. Recent Changes by AI Coding Agent
Given that the issue worsened after the AI coding agent's interventions, it's crucial to review what changes were made. The agent might have introduced new CSS rules (e.g., `overflow: hidden`) or JavaScript that disrupts scrolling. If you have version control (e.g., Git), consider reverting to a previous commit where scrolling worked and then reapply changes incrementally to identify the problematic code.

If reverting isn't feasible, compare the current code with a backup or describe the changes made (e.g., new CSS files, JavaScript functions) to pinpoint potential issues. This step is vital, as the agent's modifications likely introduced the current problems.

#### Additional Considerations
- **Fixed or Sticky Elements**: Elements with `position: fixed` can prevent interaction with underlying content, especially on mobile. Check for such elements in the admin section and ensure they don't cover scrollable areas.
- **Touch Event Handling**: On mobile, ensure touch events are handled correctly. For example, if there are swipe gestures or custom scroll behaviors, they might conflict with default scrolling.
- **Modal or Overlay Issues**: If the admin section uses modals, ensure they unlock scrolling when closed, as some libraries lock the body scroll during modal display.

#### Recommended Actions Table
Below is a table summarizing the recommended actions, their purpose, and expected outcomes:

| **Action**                          | **Purpose**                                      | **Expected Outcome**                          |
|-------------------------------------|--------------------------------------------------|----------------------------------------------|
| Use DevTools to simulate mobile view | Identify CSS and JS issues in admin section      | Pinpoint `overflow` settings or JS errors    |
| Check `overflow` property            | Ensure scrolling is enabled for containers       | Scrolling should work if set to `auto` or `scroll` |
| Disable JavaScript temporarily       | Isolate JS-related scrolling issues              | Scrolling works without JS, indicating script problem |
| Review recent code changes           | Identify AI agent's modifications causing issues | Revert or fix problematic changes            |
| Verify viewport meta tag             | Ensure proper mobile rendering                  | Improved layout and component visibility     |

#### Conclusion and Next Steps
The analysis suggests that the scrolling issue is likely due to CSS (`overflow: hidden`) or JavaScript interference, exacerbated by recent changes from the AI coding agent. By following the troubleshooting steps outlined, particularly using developer tools and reviewing code changes, you should be able to diagnose and resolve the problem. If issues persist, providing specific code snippets related to the admin section's layout and recent modifications would enable more targeted assistance.

Given the private nature of your GitHub repository, consider sharing relevant excerpts here for further analysis, ensuring sensitive information is redacted. This approach will help ensure your website functions correctly, especially on mobile devices, enhancing user experience for your client.

### **ASSISTANT**:
Below is a detailed prompt you can provide to an AI coder to address the scrolling and component display issues in the admin section of your website, particularly on mobile devices. This prompt is designed to guide the coder systematically through diagnosing and fixing the problem based on common web development practices.

---

### Prompt for AI Coder

To resolve the scrolling and component display issues in the admin section of the website [transformedacademyhq.co.uk](https://transformedacademyhq.co.uk), particularly on mobile devices like a Samsung phone, please follow these detailed steps. The issue occurs after logging into the admin section (using credentials: email `drivendatadynamics@gmail.com`, password `DCLrip7292!`), where scrolling is not functioning and components are not displaying properly. The problem worsened after recent changes by an AI coding agent, so your task is to identify and fix the root cause.

#### 1. CSS Inspection and Adjustment
- **Objective**: Ensure CSS settings allow scrolling and proper rendering on mobile.
- **Steps**:
  - Use your browser's developer tools (e.g., Chrome DevTools) to simulate a mobile device (e.g., Samsung Galaxy) and log into the admin section.
  - Inspect the `<body>` and main container elements (e.g., `<div>`, `<section>`) in the admin section. Look for any CSS rules setting `overflow: hidden` that might prevent scrolling.
  - If `overflow: hidden` is found, modify it to `overflow: auto` or `overflow: scroll` for the relevant elements to enable scrolling.
  - Verify the viewport meta tag in the HTML `<head>`. It should be set as:
    ```html
    <meta name="viewport" content="width=device-width, initial-scale=1.0">
    ```
    If missing or incorrect, add or adjust it to ensure proper mobile rendering.
- **Expected Outcome**: Scrolling should work, and the layout should adapt correctly to mobile screens.

#### 2. JavaScript Review
- **Objective**: Identify and fix any JavaScript interfering with scrolling or functionality.
- **Steps**:
  - In developer tools, open the "Console" tab and check for JavaScript errors after loading the admin section. Fix any errors that might disrupt scrolling or rendering.
  - Navigate to the "Event Listeners" tab and look for touch event handlers (e.g., `touchstart`, `touchmove`) attached to elements. If a script calls `preventDefault()` on these events, it could block scrolling—remove or adjust this behavior to allow default scrolling.
  - Temporarily disable JavaScript (e.g., via browser settings or DevTools) and test if scrolling works. If it does, the issue is JavaScript-related—locate and modify the problematic script.
- **Expected Outcome**: Scrolling functions normally without JavaScript interference.

#### 3. Layout and Component Display
- **Objective**: Ensure all components are visible and correctly positioned within the viewport.
- **Steps**:
  - In mobile view (via DevTools), inspect the layout of the admin section. Check for elements with `position: fixed` or `position: absolute` that might overlap scrollable areas or push content off-screen—adjust their positioning or z-index if needed.
  - Verify that the content height exceeds the viewport height (e.g., check computed styles in DevTools). If not, there may be no scrollable content—adjust container heights or content to ensure overflow occurs.
  - Look for CSS properties like `display: none` or `visibility: hidden` hiding components unintentionally. Adjust these to make components visible as intended.
- **Expected Outcome**: All components display correctly within the mobile viewport, and scrolling works if content overflows.

#### 4. Review Recent Code Changes
- **Objective**: Identify changes made by the AI coding agent that caused or worsened the issue.
- **Steps**:
  - Access the codebase (stored in a private GitHub repository) and review the most recent commits or changes, focusing on modifications to CSS, JavaScript, or HTML in the admin section.
  - If version control is available, revert to a commit before the AI agent's changes where scrolling worked, then reapply changes step-by-step to pinpoint the problematic update.
  - Pay special attention to new CSS rules (e.g., `overflow: hidden`) or JavaScript functions (e.g., event listeners) introduced by the AI agent that might affect scrolling or layout.
- **Expected Outcome**: The specific change causing the issue is identified and corrected, restoring functionality.

#### 5. Additional Considerations
- **Fixed/Sticky Elements**: Check for elements with `position: fixed` or `position: sticky` that might block interaction with scrollable content. Adjust their size or position if they interfere.
- **Touch Events**: Ensure touch event handling (e.g., for swipes or gestures) doesn’t conflict with default scrolling behavior on mobile.
- **Modals/Overlays**: If the admin section uses modals, verify that body scrolling is unlocked when they close—fix any locking behavior in the code.

#### Final Instructions
- Test all changes on a mobile device (e.g., your Samsung phone) and in DevTools’ mobile simulation to confirm scrolling and component display work as expected.
- If the issue persists after these steps, extract and share relevant code snippets (e.g., CSS for the admin section, recent JavaScript changes) with sensitive data redacted, so further assistance can be provided.
- Document any fixes applied for future reference, especially if reverting or modifying AI-generated code.

By following this structured approach, you should be able to diagnose and resolve the scrolling and display issues efficiently, ensuring the admin section works seamlessly on mobile devices.

## [358] Secure Website Deployment Guide
**Date:** 2025-04-16T15:07:11.973193Z

### **HUMAN**:

### **ASSISTANT**:
To secure your client's website hosted on Netlify with a GoDaddy domain and address the "not safe" warning, while also making the GitHub repository private, you need to ensure proper HTTPS setup, DNS configuration, and repository privacy. The "not safe" warning typically indicates an issue with the SSL/TLS certificate or mixed content, causing browsers to flag the site as insecure. Below is a step-by-step guide to resolve these issues and enhance security for https://transformedacademyhq.co.uk.

---

### Step 1: Make the GitHub Repository Private
Since the repository is currently public, making it private will restrict access to authorized users only. Netlify supports deploying from private repositories, even on free plans.

1. **Log in to GitHub**:
   - Go to GitHub and sign in to the account that owns the repository.

2. **Navigate to the Repository**:
   - Find the repository for your client's website (e.g., the one linked to Netlify).

3. **Access Repository Settings**:
   - Click on the **Settings** tab at the top of the repository page.

4. **Change Repository Visibility**:
   - Scroll down to the **Danger Zone** section.
   - Locate the **Change repository visibility** option.
   - Click **Change visibility** and select **Make private**.
   - Confirm the action by typing the repository name and clicking **I understand, make this repository private**.

5. **Verify Netlify Integration**:
   - Netlify should still have access to the repository if it was previously authorized.
   - Go to your Netlify dashboard (https://app.netlify.com), select your site, and navigate to **Site settings > Build & deploy > Repository**.
   - Ensure the repository is still linked. If not, reauthorize Netlify:
     - Click **Link repository** and follow the prompts to grant Netlify access to the private repository via GitHub.

6. **Test Deployment**:
   - Push a small change to the repository (e.g., update a README file) to confirm that Netlify can still deploy from the private repository without issues.

**Note**: If you’re using a free GitHub account, private repositories are supported, and Netlify’s free tier allows deployment from private repos. If you encounter permission issues, ensure Netlify’s GitHub app has access to the repository in your GitHub settings under **Applications > Authorized OAuth Apps**.

---

### Step 2: Fix the "Not Safe" Warning (Ensure HTTPS and SSL/TLS)
The "not safe" warning is likely due to an invalid or missing SSL/TLS certificate, incorrect DNS settings, or mixed content (HTTP resources on an HTTPS page). Netlify provides free SSL/TLS certificates via Let’s Encrypt, which should be enabled for your custom domain.

1. **Verify Custom Domain Setup in Netlify**:
   - Log in to your Netlify dashboard (https://app.netlify.com).
   - Select your site (e.g., the one for transformedacademyhq.co.uk).
   - Go to **Domain management** (under **Site settings > Domain management**).
   - Check that your custom domain (transformedacademyhq.co.uk) is listed under **Custom domains**.
   - If it’s not added:
     - Click **Add custom domain**.
     - Enter `transformedacademyhq.co.uk` (without www) and click **Verify**.
     - Confirm ownership by clicking **Yes, add domain**.
   - Optionally, add the www subdomain (`www.transformedacademyhq.co.uk`) by repeating the process.

2. **Check HTTPS Status**:
   - In the **Domain management** section, click on the domain (transformedacademyhq.co.uk).
   - Under **HTTPS**, ensure it says **Certificate is active** or **TLS certificate provisioned**.
   - If it says **Waiting on DNS propagation** or there’s an error:
     - Click **Verify DNS configuration**.
     - If the certificate is not provisioned, proceed to the DNS setup below.
   - If no certificate is present, click **Provision certificate** to request a Let’s Encrypt certificate. This may take a few minutes.

3. **Configure DNS Records in GoDaddy**:
   - Log in to your GoDaddy account (https://my.godaddy.com).
   - Navigate to **DNS Management** for transformedacademyhq.co.uk:
     - Find the domain in your GoDaddy dashboard.
     - Click **Manage DNS** or **DNS Records**.
   - Update the DNS records to point to Netlify. You have two options:

     **Option 1: Use Netlify’s Nameservers (Recommended)**:
     - In Netlify’s **Domain management**, find the **Name servers** section (e.g., dns1.p01.nsone.net, dns2.p01.nsone.net, etc.).
     - In GoDaddy’s DNS Management, locate the **Nameservers** section and click **Change**.
     - Select **Custom** and enter the four Netlify nameservers provided.
     - Save the changes.
     - Note: Nameserver changes can take 24–48 hours to propagate.

     **Option 2: Use GoDaddy’s Nameservers with DNS Records**:
     - If you need to keep GoDaddy’s nameservers (e.g., for email services), add the following DNS records:
       - **A Record**:
         - Type: A
         - Host: @
         - Value: 104.198.14.52 (Netlify’s load balancer IP)
         - TTL: 3600 (or default)
       - **CNAME Record** (for www subdomain):
         - Type: CNAME
         - Host: www
         - Value: your-netlify-subdomain.netlify.app (e.g., transformedacademyhq.netlify.app)
         - TTL: 3600 (or default)
     - Delete any conflicting A or CNAME records for the same hosts.
     - Save the changes.

   - **Verify DNS Propagation**:
     - Use a tool like https://www.whatsmydns.net to check if the DNS records have propagated globally.
     - Wait up to 24–48 hours for full propagation.

4. **Force HTTPS**:
   - In Netlify’s **Domain management**, under **HTTPS**, enable **Force HTTPS** to redirect all HTTP traffic to HTTPS.
   - This ensures visitors always access the secure version of the site.

5. **Check for Mixed Content**:
   - The "not safe" warning can occur if your site loads resources (e.g., images, scripts, or CSS) over HTTP instead of HTTPS.
   - Open the site in Chrome, right-click, and select **Inspect** to open Developer Tools.
   - Go to the **Console** tab and look for errors like “Mixed Content: The page was loaded over HTTPS, but requested an insecure resource.”
   - Fix mixed content:
     - Update all resource URLs in your HTML/CSS/JS to use `https://` or relative paths (e.g., `/images/example.jpg`).
     - If using external resources (e.g., APIs or CDNs), ensure they support HTTPS.
     - Push the changes to your GitHub repository to trigger a new Netlify deployment.
   - Alternatively, add a Content Security Policy (CSP) header to block insecure resources (see Step 4).

6. **Test the SSL Certificate**:
   - Visit https://www.ssllabs.com/ssltest/ and enter transformedacademyhq.co.uk.
   - Run the test to verify the SSL certificate is valid and properly configured.
   - If issues are detected, double-check DNS settings or contact Netlify support.

**Sources**:,,,,[](https://mattmilici.medium.com/connect-a-custom-godaddy-domain-to-your-netlify-site-a48aa18191d7)[](https://medium.com/%40kajol_singh/connect-your-godaddy-domain-to-netlify-d53f8758f3d0)[](https://neophyte.home.blog/2021/07/06/connect-a-godaddy-domain-to-a-netlify-website/)

---

### Step 3: Enhance Website Security
To further secure the site and prevent future warnings, implement these best practices.

1. **Add Security Headers**:
   - Create a `_headers` file in the root of your website’s deployed folder (e.g., next to `index.html` or in the `/public` folder for frameworks).
   - Add the following security headers:
     ```
     /*
       X-Frame-Options: DENY
       X-XSS-Protection: 1; mode=block
       X-Content-Type-Options: nosniff
       Referrer-Policy: no-referrer
       Strict-Transport-Security: max-age=31536000; includeSubDomains; preload
       Content-Security-Policy: default-src 'self'; img-src 'self' https:; script-src 'self'; style-src 'self' https:; font-src 'self' https:;
     ```
   - Alternatively, create a `netlify.toml` file in the root of your repository:
     ```toml
     [[headers]]
       for = "/*"
       [headers.values]
         X-Frame-Options = "DENY"
         X-XSS-Protection = "1; mode=block"
         X-Content-Type-Options = "nosniff"
         Referrer-Policy = "no-referrer"
         Strict-Transport-Security = "max-age=31536000; includeSubDomains; preload"
         Content-Security-Policy = "default-src 'self'; img-src 'self' https:; script-src 'self'; style-src 'self' https:; font-src 'self' https:;"
     ```
   - Commit and push the changes to GitHub to deploy them via Netlify.
   - These headers prevent clickjacking, XSS attacks, MIME-type sniffing, and enforce HTTPS.

2. **Enable HSTS Preload**:
   - The `Strict-Transport-Security` header above enables HTTP Strict Transport Security (HSTS).
   - Submit your domain to the HSTS preload list at https://hstspreload.org to ensure browsers always load it over HTTPS.
   - Follow the instructions to verify eligibility and submit the domain.

3. **Add a CAA Record**:
   - In GoDaddy’s DNS Management, add a Certificate Authority Authorization (CAA) record to specify that only Let’s Encrypt can issue certificates:
     - Type: CAA
     - Host: @
     - Value: 0 issue "letsencrypt.org"
     - TTL: 3600
   - This prevents unauthorized certificate issuance.

4. **Secure Environment Variables**:
   - If your site uses environment variables (e.g., API keys), store them in Netlify’s dashboard under **Site settings > Environment variables** instead of in `netlify.toml` or `.env` files in the repository.
   - This prevents accidental exposure in a public or private repository.

**Sources**:,[](https://medium.com/%40brandonl.4231/how-i-increased-the-security-of-my-netlify-hosted-website-with-this-one-small-trick-731f4c56efd7)[](https://docs.netlify.com/platform/security-checklist/)

---

### Step 4: Verify and Monitor
1. **Test the Site**:
   - Visit https://transformedacademyhq.co.uk in multiple browsers (Chrome, Firefox, Safari).
   - Ensure no "not safe" warnings appear and the padlock icon is visible in the address bar.
   - Test both the apex domain (transformedacademyhq.co.uk) and www subdomain (www.transformedacademyhq.co.uk).

2. **Monitor SSL and Security**:
   - Periodically check the SSL certificate status using https://www.ssllabs.com/ssltest/.
   - Use tools like https://securityheaders.com to verify your security headers.

3. **Set Up Alerts**:
   - In Netlify, enable notifications for deployment failures or certificate issues under **Site settings > Notifications**.
   - Monitor GoDaddy for domain renewal reminders to prevent expiration.

---

### Step 5: Troubleshooting Common Issues
- **DNS Propagation Delays**:
  - If the SSL certificate doesn’t activate, wait 24–48 hours for DNS propagation. Check progress with https://www.whatsmydns.net.
  - If it persists, contact Netlify support via the dashboard or GoDaddy support for DNS issues.

- **Mixed Content Errors**:
  - If mixed content persists, use Chrome Developer Tools to identify problematic resources and update them in your codebase.

- **Certificate Provisioning Errors**:
  - If Netlify fails to provision a certificate, ensure DNS records match Netlify’s requirements. You may need to manually trigger a certificate renewal in the **HTTPS** section of Netlify’s Domain management.

- **Email Services on GoDaddy**:
  - If your client uses GoDaddy for email and changing nameservers breaks it, use Option 2 (A and CNAME records) instead of Netlify’s nameservers. Add MX records in GoDaddy’s DNS Management to restore email functionality if needed.

**Sources**:,[](https://answers.netlify.com/t/how-to-use-godaddy-domain-with-netlify-hosted-site-while-domain-is-being-used-for-email-with-godaddy/124369)[](https://answers.netlify.com/t/website-says-it-is-unsafe/71235)

---

### Additional Notes
- **GitHub Repository Privacy**: Making the repository private doesn’t affect the deployed site’s security but protects your source code. Ensure only trusted collaborators have access.
- **GoDaddy SSL**: You don’t need a separate GoDaddy SSL certificate, as Netlify’s Let’s Encrypt certificate is sufficient and auto-renews every 90 days.[](https://connorocampo.dev/blog/custom-domain-netlify/)
- **Cost**: These steps use free features from Netlify and GitHub. No additional costs are required unless you need advanced GoDaddy services (e.g., email hosting).
- **Backup**: Before making DNS changes, export your current GoDaddy DNS records as a backup in case you need to revert.

By following these steps, you should resolve the "not safe" warning, secure the site with HTTPS, and protect the repository. If issues persist, share specific error messages or symptoms for further assistance.

### Step 3: Fix the "Not Safe" Warning (Ensure HTTPS and SSL/TLS)
The "not safe" warning typically indicates an issue with the SSL/TLS certificate, DNS configuration, or mixed content. Since your domain is registered with GoDaddy and hosted on Netlify, let’s ensure everything is set up correctly.

#### 3.1 Verify Custom Domain in Netlify
1. **Go to Domain Management**:
   - In your Netlify dashboard, navigate to **Site configuration > Domain management** (visible in your screenshot).
   - Check if `transformedacademyhq.co.uk` is listed under **Custom domains**.
   - If it’s not:
     - Click **Add custom domain**.

     - Click **Verify DNS configuration** to see suggested DNS records.
     - If no certificate is present, click **Provision certificate** to request a Let’s Encrypt certificate (this may take a few minutes).

3. **Force HTTPS**:
   - In the **HTTPS** section, enable **Force HTTPS** to redirect all HTTP traffic to HTTPS (e.g., `http://transformedacademyhq.co.uk` to `https://transformedacademyhq.co.uk`).

#### 3.2 Configure DNS Records in GoDaddy
The warning may stem from incorrect DNS settings. Netlify requires specific DNS records to enable HTTPS.

1. **Log in to GoDaddy**:
   - Go to https://my.godaddy.com and sign in.
   - Find `transformedacademyhq.co.uk` in your domain list and click **DNS > Manage DNS**.

2. **Choose a DNS Setup**:
   - **Option 1: Use Netlify’s Nameservers (Recommended)**:
     - In Netlify’s **Domain management**, find the **Name servers** section (e.g., `dns1.p01.nsone.net`, `dns2.p01.nsone.net`, etc.).
     - In GoDaddy’s DNS Management, click **Change** under **Nameservers**.
     - Select **Custom** and enter the four Netlify nameservers.
     - Save changes.
     - Note: Nameserver changes take 24–48 hours to propagate.
   - **Option 2: Use GoDaddy’s Nameservers with DNS Records**:
     - If you need GoDaddy’s nameservers (e.g., for email), add these records:
       - **A Record**:
         - Type: A
         - Host: @
         - Value: 104.198.14.52 (Netlify’s load balancer IP)
         - TTL: 3600
       - **CNAME Record** (for www):
         - Type: CNAME
         - Host: www
         - Value: transformedacademyhq.netlify.app (your Netlify subdomain, found in **Domain management**)
         - TTL: 3600
       - Delete conflicting A or CNAME records for `@` or `www`.
     - Save changes.

3. **Verify DNS Propagation**:
   - Use https://www.whatsmydns.net to check if DNS records have propagated.
   - Wait 24–48 hours if you changed nameservers.

#### 3.3 Check for Mixed Content
If the SSL certificate is active but the warning persists, mixed content (HTTP resources on an HTTPS page) may be the issue.

1. **Inspect the Site**:
   - Open https://transformedacademyhq.co.uk in Chrome.
   - Right-click and select **Inspect** to open Developer Tools.
   - Go to the **Console** tab and look for errors like “Mixed Content: The page was loaded over HTTPS, but requested an insecure resource.”

2. **Fix Mixed Content**:
   - Identify resources (e.g., images, scripts, CSS) loaded over `http://`.
   - Update your codebase:
     - Change `http://` to `https://` for external resources.
     - Use relative paths (e.g., `/images/example.jpg`) for local resources.
   - Example: If an image is loaded as `<img src="http://example.com/image.jpg">`, update to `<img src="https://example.com/image.jpg">`.
   - Commit changes to your GitHub repository to trigger a new Netlify deployment.

3. **Test Again**:
   - Clear your browser cache and revisit https://transformedacademyhq.co.uk.
   - Ensure no mixed content errors appear.

#### 3.4 Verify SSL Certificate
- Visit https://www.ssllabs.com/ssltest/ and enter `transformedacademyhq.co.uk`.
- Run the test to confirm the SSL certificate is valid.
- If errors are detected, double-check DNS settings or reprovision the certificate in Netlify.

---

### Step 4: Additional Security Measures
To prevent future issues and enhance security:

1. **Add Security Headers**:
   - Create a `_headers` file in your repository’s root (e.g., `/public/_headers` for static sites):
     ```
     /*
       X-Frame-Options: DENY
       X-XSS-Protection: 1; mode=block
       X-Content-Type-Options: nosniff
       Referrer-Policy: no-referrer
       Strict-Transport-Security: max-age=31536000; includeSubDomains; preload
       Content-Security-Policy: default-src 'self'; img-src 'self' https:; script-src 'self'; style-src 'self' https:; font-src 'self' https:;
     ```
   - Alternatively, use a `netlify.toml` file:
     ```toml
     [[headers]]
       for = "/*"
       [headers.values]
         X-Frame-Options = "DENY"
         X-XSS-Protection = "1; mode=block"
         X-Content-Type-Options = "nosniff"
         Referrer-Policy = "no-referrer"
         Strict-Transport-Security = "max-age=31536000; includeSubDomains; preload"
         Content-Security-Policy = "default-src 'self'; img-src 'self' https:; script-src 'self'; style-src 'self' https:; font-src 'self' https:;"
     ```
   - Commit and push to GitHub to deploy.

2. **Add a CAA Record in GoDaddy**:
   - In GoDaddy’s DNS Management, add:
     - Type: CAA
     - Host: @
     - Value: 0 issue "letsencrypt.org"
     - TTL: 3600
   - This restricts certificate issuance to Let’s Encrypt.

3. **Secure Environment Variables**:
   - If your site uses API keys or sensitive data, store them in **Site configuration > Environment variables** in Netlify, not in the repository.

4. **Monitor and Renew**:
   - Netlify auto-renews Let’s Encrypt certificates every 90 days.
   - Monitor GoDaddy for domain renewal to prevent expiration.

---

1. **Test the Site**:
   - Visit https://transformedacademyhq.co.uk and http://transformedacademyhq.co.uk (it should redirect to HTTPS).
   - Check for the padlock icon and no "not safe" warning.
   - Test `www.transformedacademyhq.co.uk` if configured.

2. **Troubleshooting**:
   - **DNS Issues**: If the certificate isn’t active, verify DNS records and wait for propagation. Contact Netlify support if needed.
   - **Mixed Content**: Use Chrome Developer Tools to pinpoint and fix HTTP resources.
   - **Certificate Errors**: Reprovision the certificate in Netlify or check for conflicting SSL settings in GoDaddy.

3. **Contact Support**:
   - Netlify: Use the **Support** link in the dashboard.
   - GoDaddy: Call 020 7021 3928 (UK support) or use live chat.

#### 2.2 Check for Mixed Content
Mixed content occurs when HTTPS pages load resources (e.g., images, scripts, CSS) over HTTP, triggering the "not safe" warning.

1. **Inspect the Site**:
   - Open https://transformedacademyhq.co.uk in Chrome.
   - Right-click and select **Inspect** to open Developer Tools.
   - Go to the **Console** tab and look for errors like:
     ```
     Mixed Content: The page at 'https://transformedacademyhq.co.uk/' was loaded over HTTPS, but requested an insecure resource 'http://example.com/image.jpg'. This request has been blocked; the content must be served over HTTPS.
     ```

2. **Fix Mixed Content**:
   - Identify problematic resources in the Console (e.g., images, scripts, or external APIs).
   - Update your website’s codebase in the GitHub repository:
     - Change `http://` to `https://` for external resources (e.g., `<img src="http://example.com/image.jpg">` to `<img src="https://example.com/image.jpg">`).
     - Use relative paths for local resources (e.g., `<img src="/images/image.jpg">`).
     - If using external APIs or CDNs, ensure they support HTTPS.
   - Example fix in HTML:
     ```html
     <!-- Before -->
     <img src="http://example.com/logo.png">
     <script src="http://cdn.example.com/script.js"></script>
     
     <!-- After -->
     <img src="https://example.com/logo.png">
     <script src="https://cdn.example.com/script.js"></script>
     ```
   - Commit and push changes to the GitHub repository to trigger a new Netlify deployment.

   - Clear your browser cache and revisit https://transformedacademyhq.co.uk.

### Step 4: Enhance Security with Headers
To prevent future security issues and reinforce HTTPS, add security headers to your site. This also helps mitigate mixed content by restricting resource sources.

   - Add the following content:

<xaiArtifact artifact_id="c51f7160-a865-4357-9d74-1458abf1dded" artifact_version_id="b1a454d0-3ea1-46b5-a19c-f9c0078fc83b" title="_headers" contentType="text/plain">

  X-XSS-Protection: 1; mode=block
  X-Content-Type-Options: nosniff
  Referrer-Policy: no-referrer
  Strict-Transport-Security: max-age=31536000; includeSubDomains; preload
  Content-Security-Policy: default-src 'self'; img-src 'self' https:; script-src 'self'; style-src 'self' https:; font-src 'self' https:;

     ```toml
       for = "/*"
       [headers.values]
         X-Frame-Options = "DENY"
         X-XSS-Protection = "1; mode=block"
         X-Content-Type-Options = "nosniff"
         Referrer-Policy = "no-referrer"
         Strict-Transport-Security = "max-age=31536000; includeSubDomains; preload"
         Content-Security-Policy = "default-src 'self'; img-src 'self' https:; script-src 'self'; style-src 'self' https:; font-src 'self' https:;"
     ```
   - Place `netlify.toml` in the repository root.

3. **Deploy Changes**:
